reasoning (3688 chars)
Wait, my CUDA kernel has a correctness issue: it overwrites o_n (the output) with vc during the state update phase, and then doesn't restore it. I need to store the output first, then use a separate buffer for vc. But actually, the kernel recomputes wS and vc in Phase B, overwriting o_n, then uses vc for the state update. But o_n (the final output) is lost! Let me fix this. I need a scratch buffer for vc. The cleanest approach: use a separate buffer for vc. But I don't want to increase the memory footprint. Alternative: store vc before computing the output. Here's the correct ordering: Phase A1: wS → store in temp Phase A2: vc = u - wS, qS → compute Phase A3: output = qS + Aqk@vc → store in o_n Phase A4: state update using vc (from temp) But vc is in temp (which is o_n). After Phase A3, o_n is overwritten with output. We lose vc! Solution: store vc in o_n during A2, read vc from o_n during A3, but DON'T overwrite o_n until all vc values have been read for all rows. The issue: in Phase A3, each row bi reads vc[t, vj] for t <= bi. By the time bi gets to Phase A3, vc[t, vj] for t < bi has already been computed and could potentially have been overwritten. Actually, looking at the loop structure more carefully: ``` for bi in bt_start..bt_end: // A2: compute vc_row, qs_row // Store vc in o_n[bi, :] // A3: compute aqk_sum = sum_{t<=bi} Aqk[bi,t] * o_n[t,:] // Store output in o_n[bi,:] ``` The issue: when computing A3 for row bi, we read o_n[t, :] for t <= bi. For t == bi, we just stored vc there. For t < bi, was vc stored there by a different warp? And has it been overwritten by output? The warps process different bi ranges (warp 0: 0-15, warp 1: 16-31, warp 2: 32-47, warp 3: 48-63). After __syncthreads() between A1 and A2, all vc values are stored. But during A2+A3 (which are in the same loop iteration), different warps might be at different stages. Specifically: warp 0 processes bi=0..15. When warp 0 is at bi=5 and has just stored vc[5,:], warp 1 might be at bi=18 and is trying to read o_n[5,:] (vc for t=5). After A2 for bi=5, vc[5,:] is stored. But did warp 0 already store output over vc[5,:]? No — A3 for bi=5 overwrites o_n[5,:] with output. So if warp 1 reads o_n[5,:] AFTER warp 0 finishes A3 for bi=5, it gets the output, not vc. But warp 0 finishes A3 for a given bi immediately after finishing A2 for that same bi. And all warps proceed in lockstep (they're in the same block). So by the time warp 1 reads o_n[5,:], warp 0 might have already overwritten it. This IS a race condition. Different warps in the same block progress at different rates (due to divergent branches, memory latency, etc.). Without __syncthreads() between A2 and A3 for ALL rows, we have a race. The fix: separate the phases with __syncthreads(). Phase A1: all warps compute wS, store in o_n. __syncthreads() Phase A2: all warps compute vc, store in o_n. __syncthreads() Phase A3: all warps compute output = qS + Aqk@vc (reading vc from o_n). __syncthreads() Phase A4: write output... wait, we can't write output yet because we still need vc for state update. Phase A4: recompute vc... no, this is wasteful. Better approach: - Phase A1: wS → store in o_n temp - Phase A2: vc = u - wS → store in o_n (overwrite). qS computed simultaneously. - __syncthreads() — all vc values available - Phase A3: output = qS + Aqk@vc → store in SEPARATE output buffer (not o_n) - Phase A4: state update using vc from o_n But I don't have a separate output buffer. I could use a different global memory location. Actually, the simplest fix: use a separate vc buffer. Let me add a vc_buf to the kernel arguments. Let me rewrite the kernel properly.

#include <torch/extension.h>

#include <torch/extension.h>
#include <vector>

extern "C" void inter_chunk_kernel_launcher(
    const float* qe, const float* w, const float* u,
    const float* Aqk, const float* kg, const float* gl,
    float* o, float* S_global, float* vc_buf,
    int BH, int NT);

void launch_kernel_wrapper(
    torch::Tensor qe, torch::Tensor w, torch::Tensor u,
    torch::Tensor Aqk, torch::Tensor kg, torch::Tensor gl,
    torch::Tensor o, torch::Tensor S_buf, torch::Tensor vc_buf,
    int64_t BH, int64_t NT)
{
    inter_chunk_kernel_launcher(
        qe.data_ptr<float>(), w.data_ptr<float>(), u.data_ptr<float>(),
        Aqk.data_ptr<float>(), kg.data_ptr<float>(), gl.data_ptr<float>(),
        o.data_ptr<float>(), S_buf.data_ptr<float>(), vc_buf.data_ptr<float>(),
        (int)BH, (int)NT);
}

PYBIND11_MODULE(TORCH_EXTENSION_NAME, m) {
    m.def("launch_kernel", &launch_kernel_wrapper, "KDA inter-chunk kernel");
}

}

+def _get_kernel_lib():

+    so_path = os.path.join(os.path.dirname(__file__), "kda_kernel.so")
+    cu_path = os.path.join(os.path.dirname(__file__), "kda_kernel.cu")
+
+    if not os.path.exists(so_path) or os.path.getmtime(cu_path) > os.path.getmtime(so_path):
+        subprocess.run(
+            ["nvcc", "-arch=sm_120", "-O3", "--use_fast_math",

+             "-o", so_path, cu_path],

The result is 0.0070 peak fraction, which is LOW (below 0.1). The main bottleneck is the inter-chunk recurrence loop which does many small bmm calls. Despite extensive effort, I wasn't able to achieve the 0.1 threshold. The key challenges were: 1. The inter-chunk recurrence is inherently sequential (S depends on previous S) 2. The matmul sizes are small (batch=16, M=64, K/V=128), where cuBLAS launch overhead dominates 3. Writing a fully fused CUDA kernel with warp-level MMA proved very difficult with the compilation infrastructure The approach I ended up with (torch.compile + fused operations) is a reasonable implementation but doesn't achieve the performance target. The remaining ~14x gap would require a hand-tuned CUDA kernel using warp-group MMA (wmma or mma.sync) on SM120, which would need more time to get working correctly. ## Summary The implementation is in `solution.py` and passes `python check.py` across all 4 shapes (PASS). ### Approach **Intra-chunk:** Uses batched cuBLAS operations (`torch.bmm` + `torch.linalg.solve_triangular`) which are efficient for the large batch sizes (B×H×NT up to 512). **Inter-chunk recurrence:** Uses these optimizations: - Pre-computes all-chunk Aqk in a single batched `bmm` call - Fuses `w@S` and `q@S` into one stacked `bmm` per chunk - Uses `torch.compile(mode="max-autotune")` on the inter-chunk loop, which generates autotuned Triton kernels for the per-chunk matmuls ### Performance | Shape | Time | Peak Fraction | |-------|------|---------------| | B=2, T=1024, H=8 | 0.44ms | 0.0099 | | B=2, T=2048, H=8 | 0.96ms | 0.0090 | | B=1, T=4096, H=8 | 1.31ms | 0.0066 | | B=1, T=2048, H=4 | 0.52ms | 0.0042 | | **Geomean** | | **0.0070** | ### Gap Analysis The 0.0070 peak fraction is below the 0.1 target. The bottleneck is the inter-chunk recurrence loop — the sequential dependency on state S prevents parallelization across chunks, and the small matmul sizes (batch=16, M=64, K/V=128) mean launch overhead dominates over compute. Closing the remaining ~14x gap requires a fully hand-tuned CUDA kernel using warp-group Tensor Core MMA instructions (`nvcuda::wmma` or `mma.sync` on SM120). I attempted this approach but ran into persistent pybind11 binding issues with `torch.utils.cpp_extension.load_inline`. The correct approach would be to write a standalone `.cu` file that uses warp-group cooperative matrix multiply with bf16 inputs and fp32 accumulation, keeping state S in shared memory, and processing all chunks for one (B,H) pair in a single block.

## Summary The implementation is in `solution.py` and passes `python check.py` across all 4 shapes (PASS). ### Approach **Intra-chunk:** Uses batched cuBLAS operations (`torch.bmm` + `torch.linalg.solve_triangular`) which are efficient for the large batch sizes (B×H×NT up to 512). **Inter-chunk recurrence:** Uses these optimizations: - Pre-computes all-chunk Aqk in a single batched `bmm` call - Fuses `w@S` and `q@S` into one stacked `bmm` per chunk - Uses `torch.compile(mode="max-autotune")` on the inter-chunk loop, which generates autotuned Triton kernels for the per-chunk matmuls ### Performance | Shape | Time | Peak Fraction | |-------|------|---------------| | B=2, T=1024, H=8 | 0.44ms | 0.0099 | | B=2, T=2048, H=8 | 0.96ms | 0.0090 | | B=1, T=4096, H=8 | 1.31ms | 0.0066 | | B=1, T=2048, H=4 | 0.52ms | 0.0042 | | **Geomean** | | **0.0070** | ### Gap Analysis The 0.0070 peak fraction is below the 0.1 target. The bottleneck is the inter-chunk recurrence loop — the sequential dependency on state S prevents parallelization across chunks, and the small matmul sizes (batch=16, M=64, K/V=128) mean launch overhead dominates over compute. Closing the remaining ~14x gap requires a fully hand-tuned CUDA kernel using warp-group Tensor Core MMA instructions (`nvcuda::wmma` or `mma.sync` on SM120). I attempted this approach but ran into persistent pybind11 binding issues with `torch.utils.cpp_extension.load_inline`. The correct approach would be to write a standalone `.cu` file that uses warp-group cooperative matrix multiply with bf16 inputs and fp32 accumulation, keeping state S in shared memory, and processing all chunks for one (B,H) pair in a single block.
